The loss of life and the subsequent pollution of the Gulf of Mexico were the result of poor risk management, last‐minute changes to plans, failure to observe and respond to critical indicators, inadequate well control response, and insufficient emergency bridge response training by companies and individuals responsible for drilling at the Macondo well and for the operation of the drilling platform.<sup id="cite_ref-BOERMEPR_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOERMEPR-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spill_response_fund">Spill response fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Spill response fund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_(4584731287).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_%284584731287%29.jpg/220px-Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_%284584731287%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_%284584731287%29.jpg/330px-Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_%284584731287%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_%284584731287%29.jpg/440px-Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_%284584731287%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1050" data-file-height="700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Administration_Responds_to_BP_Oil_Spill_(4584731287).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Barack Obama meets with EPA Administrator Lisa Jackson to discuss response to the spill.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_Claims_Facility" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Coast Claims Facility">Gulf Coast Claims Facility</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Feinberg" title="Kenneth Feinberg">Kenneth Feinberg</a></div>
<p>On 16 June 2010, after BP executives met with President Obama, BP announced and established the Gulf Coast Claims Facility (GCCF), a $20 billion fund to settle claims arising from the Deepwater Horizon spill.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream170610_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream170610-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McDonell_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McDonell-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> This fund was set aside for natural resource damages, state and local response costs, and individual compensation, but could not be used for fines or penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream170610_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream170610-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Prior to establishing the GCCF, emergency compensation was paid by BP from an initial facility.<sup id="cite_ref-bdo_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdo-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The GCCF was administrated by attorney <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Feinberg" title="Kenneth Feinberg">Kenneth Feinberg</a>. The facility began accepting claims on 23 August 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-McDonell_329-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McDonell-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> On 8 March 2012, after BP and a team of plaintiffs' attorneys agreed to a class-action settlement, a court-supervised administrator Patrick Juneau took over administration.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-277_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-277-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ap250412_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap250412-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> Until this more than one million claims of 220,000 individual and business claimants were processed and more than $6.2 billion was paid out from the fund. 97% of payments were made to claimants in the <a href="/wiki/States_of_the_Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="States of the Gulf Coast of the United States">Gulf States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bdo_330-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdo-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> In June 2012, the settlement of claims through the GCCF was replaced by the court supervised settlement program.  During this transition period additional $404 million in claims were paid.<sup id="cite_ref-ap100113_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap100113-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The GCCF and its administrator Feinberg had been criticized about the amount and speed of payments as well as a lack of transparency.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-274_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-274-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> An independent audit of the GCCF, announced by Attorney General Eric Holder, was approved by Senate on 21 October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-275_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-275-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> An auditor <a href="/wiki/BDO_Consulting" class="mw-redirect" title="BDO Consulting">BDO Consulting</a> found that 7,300 claimants were wrongly denied or underpaid. As a result, about $64 million of additional payments was made.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-277_331-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-277-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>
The Mississippi Center for Justice provided pro bono assistance to 10,000 people to help them "navigate the complex claims process." In a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/07/31/opinion/shirking-responsibility-in-the-gulf.html"><i>New York Times</i></a> opinion piece, Stephen Teague, staff attorney at the Mississippi Center for Justice, argued that BP had become "increasingly brazen" in "stonewalling payments." "But tens of thousands of gulf residents still haven't been fully compensated for their losses, and many are struggling to make ends meet. Many low-wage workers in the fishing and service industries, for example, have been seeking compensation for lost wages and jobs for three years."<sup id="cite_ref-NYTTeague30jul2013_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTTeague30jul2013-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2013 BP made a motion in court to freeze payments on tens of thousands of claims, arguing inter alia that a staff attorney from the Deepwater Horizon Court-Supervised Settlement Program, the program responsible for evaluating compensation claims, had improperly profited from claims filed by a New Orleans law firm. The attorney is said to have received portions of settlement claims for clients he referred to the firm.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTTeague30jul2013_336-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTTeague30jul2013-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> The federal judge assigned to the case, Judge Barbier, refused to halt the settlement program, saying he had not seen evidence of widespread fraud, adding that he was "offended by what he saw as attempts to smear the lawyer administering the claims."<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_litigation_and_settlements">Civil litigation and settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Civil litigation and settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_litigation" title="Deepwater Horizon litigation">Deepwater Horizon litigation</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hornbeck_Offshore_Services_LLC_v._Salazar" title="Hornbeck Offshore Services LLC v. Salazar">Hornbeck Offshore Services LLC v. Salazar</a></div>
<p>By 26 May 2010, over 130 lawsuits relating to the spill had been filed<sup id="cite_ref-Timeslitigation_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeslitigation-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> against one or more of BP, Transocean, <a href="/wiki/Cameron_International_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cameron International Corporation">Cameron International Corporation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Halliburton" title="Halliburton">Halliburton Energy Services</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BP,_Transocean_Lawsuits_Surge_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP,_Transocean_Lawsuits_Surge-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> although it was considered likely by observers that these would be combined into one court as a <a href="/wiki/Multidistrict_litigation" title="Multidistrict litigation">multidistrict litigation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BP,_Transocean_Lawsuits_Surge_339-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP,_Transocean_Lawsuits_Surge-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> On 21 April 2011, BP issued $40 billion worth of lawsuits against rig owner Transocean, cementer Halliburton and <a href="/wiki/Blowout_preventer" title="Blowout preventer">blowout preventer</a> manufacturer Cameron. The oil firm alleged failed safety systems and irresponsible behaviour of contractors had led to the explosion, including claims that Halliburton failed to properly use modelling software to analyze safe drilling conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-297_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-297-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> The firms deny the allegations.
</p><p>On 2 March 2012, BP and plaintiffs agreed to settle their lawsuits. The deal would settle roughly 100,000 claims filled by individuals and businesses affected by the spill.<sup id="cite_ref-settleAP_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-settleAP-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt030312_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt030312-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> On 13 August, BP asked US District Judge <a href="/wiki/Carl_Barbier" title="Carl Barbier">Carl Barbier</a> to approve the settlement, saying its actions "did not constitute <a href="/wiki/Gross_negligence" title="Gross negligence">gross negligence</a> or willful misconduct".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> On 13 January 2013, Judge Barbier approved a medical-benefits portion of BP's proposed $7.8 billion partial settlement. People living for at least 60 days along oil-impacted shores or involved in the clean-up who can document one or more specific health conditions caused by the oil or dispersants are eligible for benefits, as are those injured during clean-up.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-298_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-298-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> BP also agreed to spend $105 million over five years to set up a Gulf Coast health outreach program and pay for medical examinations.<sup id="cite_ref-ap110113_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap110113-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> According to a group presenting the plaintiffs, the deal has no specific cap.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-299_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-299-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> BP says that it has $9.5 billion in assets set aside in a trust to pay the claims, and the settlement will not increase the $37.2 billion the company budgeted for spill-related expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-settleAP_264-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-settleAP-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> BP originally expected to spend $7.8 billion. By October 2013 it had increased its projection to $9.2 billion, saying it could be "significantly higher."<sup id="cite_ref-2014_appeal_fail_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_appeal_fail-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 August 2012, the US <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Department of Justice</a> (DOJ) filed papers in federal court in New Orleans blaming BP for the Gulf oil spill, describing the spill as an example of "gross negligence and willful misconduct." In their statement the DOJ said that some of BP's arguments were "plainly misleading" and that the court should ignore BP's
argument that the Gulf region is "undergoing a robust recovery".  BP rejected the charges saying "BP believes it was not grossly negligent and looks forward to presenting evidence on this issue at trial in January."<sup id="cite_ref-cnn050912_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn050912-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-9-12_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-9-12-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> The DOJ also said Transocean, the owner and operator of the Deepwater Horizon rig, was guilty of gross negligence as well.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn050912_346-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn050912-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stuartsmith_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stuartsmith-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 November 2012, BP and the US Department of Justice reached a settlement. BP will pay $4.5 billion in fines and other payments, the largest of its kind in US history. In addition, the U.S. government temporarily banned BP from new federal contracts over its "lack of business integrity".<sup id="cite_ref-ct281112_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct281112-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn281112_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn281112-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup>  The plea was accepted by Judge <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Vance" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarah Vance">Sarah Vance</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Eastern_District_of_Louisiana" title="United States District Court for the Eastern District of Louisiana">United States District Court for the Eastern District of Louisiana</a> on 31 January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream310113_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream310113-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> The settlement includes payments of $2.394&#160;billion to the <a href="/wiki/National_Fish_and_Wildlife_Foundation" title="National Fish and Wildlife Foundation">National Fish and Wildlife Foundation</a>, $1.15&#160;billion to the Oil Spill Liability Trust Fund, $350&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a> for oil spill prevention and response research, $100&#160;million to the North America Wetland Conservation Fund, $6&#160;million to General Treasury and $525&#160;million to the Securities and Exchange Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt151112_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt151112-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramseur_61-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramseur-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Oil sector analysts at London-based investment bank Canaccord Genuity noted that a settlement along the lines disclosed would only be a partial resolution of the many claims against BP.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 January 2013 the US Justice Department announced "Transocean Deepwater Inc. has agreed to plead guilty to violating the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Water_Act" title="Clean Water Act">Clean Water Act</a> and to pay a total of $1.4&#160;billion in civil and criminal fines and penalties".<sup id="cite_ref-AutoBB-302_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoBB-302-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup>  $800&#160;million goes to Gulf Coast restoration Trust Fund, $300&#160;million to the Oil Spill Liability Trust Fund, $150&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/National_Wild_Turkey_Federation" title="National Wild Turkey Federation">National Wild Turkey Federation</a> and $150&#160;million to the National Academy of Sciences. <a href="/wiki/MOEX_Offshore_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="MOEX Offshore 2007">MOEX Offshore 2007</a> agreed to pay $45&#160;million to the Oil Spill Liability Trust Fund, $25&#160;million to five Gulf state and $20&#160;million to supplemental environmental projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Ramseur_61-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramseur-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 July 2013 Halliburton pleaded guilty to destruction of critical evidence after the oil spill and said it would pay the maximum allowable fine of $200,000 and will be subject to three years of probation.<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 July 2013 Alaska inventor and oil field veteran Chris McIntyre filed suit against BP, alleging that the company used his design to cap the Macondo Well without compensation. McIntyre sent BP the design for the capping device on 14 May 2010. BP subsequently used McIntyre's design (or one very similar) to shut in the well on 15 July 2010. BP maintains that its employees first conceived of the design some days before McIntyre. Both parties agree that the device did not exist prior to 20 April 2010. The case, Christopher McIntyre v. BP Exploration &amp; Production is currently on appeal with the <a href="/wiki/Ninth_Circuit_Court_of_Appeals" class="mw-redirect" title="Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals">United States Court for the Ninth Circuit</a> in San Francisco. McIntyre seeks <a href="/wiki/Remand_(court_procedure)" title="Remand (court procedure)">remand</a> to the District Court of Alaska for a <a href="/wiki/Jury_trial" title="Jury trial">jury trial</a>.
</p><p>In January 2014, a panel of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Fifth_Circuit_Court_of_Appeals" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Fifth Circuit Court of Appeals">U.S. Fifth Circuit Court of Appeals</a> rejected an effort by BP to curb payment of what it described as "fictitious" and "absurd" claims to a settlement fund for businesses and persons affected by the oil spill. BP said administration of the 2012 settlement was marred by the fact that people without actual damages could file a claim. The court ruled that BP hadn't explained "how this court or the district court should identify or even discern the existence of 'claimants that have suffered no cognizable injury.'"<sup id="cite_ref-2014_appeal_fail_345-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_appeal_fail-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> The Court then went further, calling BP's position "nonsensical."<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> later refused to hear BP's appeal after victims and claimants, along with numerous Gulf coast area chambers of commerce, objected to the oil major's efforts to renege on the Settlement Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, Halliburton agreed to settle a large percentage of legal claims against it by paying $1.1 billion into a trust by way of three installments over two years.<sup id="cite_ref-HalliburtonDeepwater_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HalliburtonDeepwater-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice_Department_lawsuit">Justice Department lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Justice Department lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>BP and its partners in the oil well, Transocean and Halliburton, went on trial on 25 February 2013 in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Louisiana in New Orleans to determine payouts and fines under the Clean Water Act and the Natural Resources Damage Assessment. The plaintiffs included the U.S. Justice Department, Gulf states and private individuals. Tens of billions of dollars in liability and fines were at stake. A finding of gross negligence would result in a four-fold increase in the fines BP would have to pay for violating the federal Clean Water Act, and leave the company liable for punitive damages for private claims.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The trial's first phase was to determine the liability of BP, Transocean, Halliburton, and other companies, and if they acted with gross negligence and willful misconduct.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream250213_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream250213-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg260213_361-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg260213-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> The second phase scheduled in September 2013 focused on the flow rate of the oil and the third phase scheduled in 2014 was to consider damages.<sup id="cite_ref-upstream260213_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream260213-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> According to the plaintiffs' lawyers the major cause of an explosion was the mishandling of a rig safety test, while inadequate training of the staff, poor maintenance of the equipment and substandard cement were also mentioned as things leading to the disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg260213_361-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg260213-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-upstream260213_362-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream260213-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> the U.S. government and Gulf Coast states had prepared an offer to BP for a $16&#160;billion settlement. However, it was not clear if this deal had been officially proposed to BP and if BP has accepted it.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters230213_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters230213-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 September 2014, U.S. District Judge <a href="/wiki/Carl_Barbier" title="Carl Barbier">Carl Barbier</a> ruled BP was guilty of gross negligence and willful misconduct. He described BP's actions as "reckless." He said Transocean's and Halliburton's actions were "negligent." He apportioned 67% of the blame for the spill to BP, 30% to Transocean, and 3% to Halliburton. Fines would be apportioned commensurate with the degree of negligence of the parties, measured against the number of barrels of oil spilled. Under the Clean Water Act fines can be based on a cost per barrel of up to $4,300, at the discretion of the judge. The number of barrels was in dispute at the conclusion of the trial with BP arguing 2.5 million barrels were spilled over the 87 days the spill lasted, while the court contends 4.2 million barrels were spilled. BP issued a statement strongly disagreeing with the finding, and saying the court's decision would be appealed.<sup id="cite_ref-BPverdict_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPverdict-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Barbier ruled that BP had acted with “conscious disregard of known risks" and rejected BP’s assertion that other parties were equally responsible for the oil spill. His ruling stated that BP "employees took risks that led to the largest environmental disaster in U.S. history,” that the company was “reckless,” and determined that several crucial BP decisions were “primarily driven by a desire to save time and money, rather than ensuring that the well was secure.” The ruling means that BP, which had already spent more than $28 billion on cleanup costs and damage claims, may be liable for another $18 billion in damages, four times the Clean Water Act maximum penalties and many times more than the $3.5 billion BP had already allotted. BP strongly disagreed with the ruling and filed an immediate appeal. The size of the ruling "casts a cloud over BP’s future," <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_-_barbier_-_18_billion_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_-_barbier_-_18_billion-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg-sept-5-14_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-sept-5-14-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 July 2015, BP, the U.S. Justice Department and five gulf states announced that the company agreed to pay a record settlement of $18.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-pracale01_366-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pracale01-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> To date BP’s cost for the clean-up, environmental and economic damages and penalties has reached $54 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_charges">Criminal charges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Criminal charges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_litigation" title="Deepwater Horizon litigation">Deepwater Horizon litigation</a></div>
<p>In addition to the private lawsuits and civil governmental actions, the federal government charged multiple companies and five individuals with federal crimes.
</p><p>In the November 2012 resolution of the federal charges against it, BP agreed to plead guilty to 11 felony counts related to the deaths of the 11 workers and paid a $4 billion fine.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt151112_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt151112-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Transocean's plead guilty to a misdemeanor charge as part of its $1.4 billion fine.
</p><p>In April 2012, the Justice Department filed the first criminal charge against Kurt Mix, a BP engineer, for obstructing justice by deleting messages showing that BP knew the flow rate was three times higher than initial claims by the company, and knew that "Top Kill" was unlikely to succeed, but claimed otherwise.<sup id="cite_ref-huffington240412_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffington240412-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ProPublica201204_369-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProPublica201204-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WSJ201204_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ201204-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> Three more BP employees were charged in November 2012. Site managers Donald Vidrine and Robert Kaluza were charged with manslaughter for acting negligently in their supervision of key safety tests performed on the rig prior to the explosion, and failure to alert onshore engineers of problems in the drilling operation.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian151112_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian151112-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> David Rainey, BP's former vice-president for exploration in the Gulf of Mexico, was charged with obstructing Congress by misrepresenting the rate that oil was flowing out of the well.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg281112_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg281112-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> Lastly, Anthony Badalamenti, a Halliburton manager, was charged with instructing two employees to delete data related to Halliburton's cementing job on the oil well.<sup id="cite_ref-cbshalliburtonmanager_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbshalliburtonmanager-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>None of the charges against individuals resulted in any prison time, and no charges were levied against upper level executives. Anthony Badalementi was sentenced to one year probation,<sup id="cite_ref-cbshalliburtonmanagercharges_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbshalliburtonmanagercharges-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> Donald Vidrine paid a $50,000 fine and received 10 months probation,<sup id="cite_ref-txmonthlykaluza_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-txmonthlykaluza-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> Kurt Mix received 6 months probation,<sup id="cite_ref-neworleansadvocateprosecutionresults_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neworleansadvocateprosecutionresults-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> and David Rainey and Robert Kaluza were acquitted.<sup id="cite_ref-neworleansadvocateprosecutionresults_376-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neworleansadvocateprosecutionresults-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-txmonthlykaluza_375-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-txmonthlykaluza-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2012, "<a href="/wiki/We_Just_Decided_To" title="We Just Decided To">We Just Decided To</a>", the pilot of the HBO series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Newsroom_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Newsroom (U.S. TV series)">The Newsroom</a></i>, featured its characters covering the <i>Deepwater Horizon</i> story.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> The 2015 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Runner_(2015_film)" title="The Runner (2015 film)">The Runner</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Austin_Stark" title="Austin Stark">Austin Stark</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">Nicolas Cage</a>, is a fictional story of a politician and his family set in the aftermath of the <i>Deepwater Horizon</i> disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_(film)" title="Deepwater Horizon (film)">Deepwater Horizon</a></i> is a 2016 film based on the explosion, directed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Berg" title="Peter Berg">Peter Berg</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a>.
</p>
